  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3eee8d69-256d-4253-bef6-82b2a1be37bb'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer17183501607797454338">This one was definitely better than the first and I think I give that credit to Jacob - who is by far the best character to come out of this series so far. I like how the author kept him very secretive literally up until the last minute. I don't think there was really one thing I didn't like about him.<br/><br/>Now, as for everyone else...I like PJ, he's entertaining and always good for a laugh. Amber, I really just don't get. Chad - no comment. Drea - hmph...bitch and worst friend ever (I don't think my </span>
  <span id="freeText17183501607797454338" style="display:none">This one was definitely better than the first and I think I give that credit to Jacob - who is by far the best character to come out of this series so far. I like how the author kept him very secretive literally up until the last minute. I don't think there was really one thing I didn't like about him.<br /><br />Now, as for everyone else...I like PJ, he's entertaining and always good for a laugh. Amber, I really just don't get. Chad - no comment. Drea - hmph...bitch and worst friend ever (I don't think my opinion of her is ever going to change).<br /><br />The story line of this book felt a little more suspensful than the first book and I think because it had to deal with Stacey directly and her possible death. I still wish Stacey would grow a backbone though and actually stand up for herself. <br /><br />Moving onto #3...</span>

    <a title="Alley Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5010782-alley-kat"><img alt="Alley Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496525768p2/5010782.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2035342603" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7463494321069699122">I was worried about reading this since it's been so long since I read the first book, but everything was recapped very nicely. White is for Magic is a great sequel and carries on the story easily. The characters are crazy and amazing, and it all felt really believable. While I'm not a fan of romance, I like how it was done in this book. It didn't feel rushed at all like most young adult novels these days. The plot was captivating and interesting. I'm excited to read the rest of the series.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1064077959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4009479349483624205">This and other reviews can be found on <a href='http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Psychotic Nerd</a><br/><br/><b>
  <u>MY THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br/>This is going to sound very odd, but this series is like thriller candy! I enjoy reading these books!<br/><br/>This book is the sequel to Blue is for Nightmares and Stacey cannot get a break.After the murders and nightmares of last year, Stacey is dating Chase and trying at a sense of normalcy. But then the nightmares return. This time, it focuses of her past. On the girl she babysat once, but dies, and the girl who died last year. St</span>
  <span id="freeText4009479349483624205" style="display:none">This and other reviews can be found on <a href="http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Psychotic Nerd</a><br /><br /><b>
  <u>MY THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br />This is going to sound very odd, but this series is like thriller candy! I enjoy reading these books!<br /><br />This book is the sequel to Blue is for Nightmares and Stacey cannot get a break.After the murders and nightmares of last year, Stacey is dating Chase and trying at a sense of normalcy. But then the nightmares return. This time, it focuses of her past. On the girl she babysat once, but dies, and the girl who died last year. Stacey has to figure out what her nightmares are trying to tell her, along with figuring out a new student's, Jacob, motives.<br /><br />This series, as I'm sure you're aware of, is a nice mixture of thriller and paranormal. Stacey is a witch and does do spells, used herbs, candles, and mixtures. The paranormal element of this series is very unique to the thriller genre and it doesn't upright make this book unrealistic. I can actually believe that Stacey is a witch, while do believing that the events in this book are completely realistic. <br /><br />My issue with the plot would have to be the fact that it's a very common thriller. This might just be me though, as thrillers generally don't thrill me (hahaha). The plot line is very similar to other thriller books and that's one of my issue with thrillers in general. I still like them and I do enjoy reading them. While the plot is very common, it still had a sense of mystery and I didn't know what was to come!<br /><br />As far as romance, this is a great series that realistically portrays romance. The romance does not takeover the book, just like romance shouldn't take over someone's life. Stacey and Chase's relationship is also rocky. I actually like this because most YA books have forever romances, where the love interest is always the love interest. I also didn't really like them together in the first place. I'm kind of shipping Stacey and Jacob...<br /><br /><b>
  <u>IN CONCLUSION</u>
</b><br />This is a great continuation to the series. As I said, this is thriller candy. I enjoy reading these books, but they are not favorites of mine. This book has the common thriller plot, with a paranormal twist, which I did like, but didn't wow me. I do recommend continuing this series.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1852223649173786500">What would you do if one of your friends has really bad nightmares and suffering from that all night? Stacey Brown is the one who has really bad nightmares and can predict the future. A year before, Stacey Brown had saved her best friend, Drea, from a death through the nightmares.   <span id="freeText1852223649173786500" style="display:none">What would you do if one of your friends has really bad nightmares and suffering from that all night? Stacey Brown is the one who has really bad nightmares and can predict the future. A year before, Stacey Brown had saved her best friend, Drea, from a death through the nightmares. Now, she is having nightmares again about something. One day, she meet guy named Jacob. And he said he is from Colorado and having nightmares about Stacey so he moved to here, where Stacey lives, to save her. First time, Stacey didn’t believe Jacob but Jacob is the one who really helped Stacey when she was in the danger. Jacob is really interesting character because he was the one who saved Stacey and can understand her because of their nightmares. I like Stacey but if I were Stacey, I would think about my nightmares joyfully. It’s kind of creepy when I have a nightmare but I would like to think about it. Laurie Stolarz did a great job on writing story in interesting way and little mysterious but I hope Jacob has more part to him than Stacey. I recommend this book to anyone who likes mysteries and magic. This book is for all ages. Genre of this book is realistic fiction and mystery. And compare to Blue is for Nightmares, I really enjoyed White is for Magic because two reasons. New character, Jacob is new and he is really interesting character. And second, if you read Blue is for Nightmares, you can understand this book more easily. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5349200147669022091">This book was alright. Not quite as good as the first in my opinion, but okay enough. I’m going to be completely honest here and say that going into this series, I had such high hopes for it, and while there’s nothing actually wrong with the storyline, or the writing or anything like that.....it just seems to me like it falls short. I can’t exactly put my finger on what it is that the book is lacking, and while I want to love it, I really do...... I just can’t. There are some parts in the story </span>
  <span id="freeText5349200147669022091" style="display:none">This book was alright. Not quite as good as the first in my opinion, but okay enough. I’m going to be completely honest here and say that going into this series, I had such high hopes for it, and while there’s nothing actually wrong with the storyline, or the writing or anything like that.....it just seems to me like it falls short. I can’t exactly put my finger on what it is that the book is lacking, and while I want to love it, I really do...... I just can’t. There are some parts in the story where I just find myself incredibly bored and I want nothing more than for it to be finished. There’s something missing and I don’t know what it is. It leaves me frustrated. <br />The story as usual was filled with mystery and keeps you guessing as to just what the clues mean until the last minute. <br />Stacey was as cool as she was in the first book, although at times I felt like she spent too much time focusing on things that weren’t important instead of just taking action. After how the last book ended, I will say I was slightly disappointed to see how downhill Stacey’s and Chad’s relationship had gone. However I found I did like Jacob, and I look forward to seeing how his relationship with Stacey progresses. I think Drea and Chad should be together, they seem good for one another.<br /> <br />I’ll read the rest of the series, seeing as I already bought the books, but I don’t think I’m as desperate to as I was with other books. <br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16555550028993436461">Ugh.<br/><br/>This is one of the few books where I just said to myself "ok, that's it. I give up." and tossed it away.<br/>I stumbled accross the third book of the series <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/493123.Silver_Is_for_Secrets__Blue_is_for_Nightmares___3_' title='Silver Is for Secrets (Blue is for Nightmares, #3) by Laurie Faria Stolarz' rel='nofollow noopener'>Silver Is for Secrets</a> months ago, not knowing it was part of a series and I loved it.   <span id="freeText16555550028993436461" style="display:none">Ugh.<br /><br />This is one of the few books where I just said to myself "ok, that's it. I give up." and tossed it away.<br />I stumbled accross the third book of the series <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/493123.Silver_Is_for_Secrets__Blue_is_for_Nightmares___3_" title="Silver Is for Secrets (Blue is for Nightmares, #3) by Laurie Faria Stolarz" rel="nofollow noopener">Silver Is for Secrets</a> months ago, not knowing it was part of a series and I loved it. The first book was OK, I'll give Stolarz this, the storyline was exciting, the characters were not the most interesting but were funny and (kinda) likeable , it was full of suspense etc. The second book just ruined it with a storyline just a little too close to the first book, and characters with terrible personalities. I can't review the entire book since a) I didn't finish it and b) I don't particularly enjoy reviewing a book I didn't like but I'll just add that if you really want to read this series you might aswell skip this book.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12918512531838896889">Great book. Gives a lot of interesting details about spells and so separates itself from other teen books with an unusually gifted teenager. Loved the inclusion of Jacob. The book wraps you up in its mystery so that you're racing to get to the end, just like the first one. The killer's easier to pick out in this one than in the first book, though.<br/><br/>The one thing I have a beef with is that being a Christian, I hate seeing God's name uncapitalized.   <span id="freeText12918512531838896889" style="display:none">Great book. Gives a lot of interesting details about spells and so separates itself from other teen books with an unusually gifted teenager. Loved the inclusion of Jacob. The book wraps you up in its mystery so that you're racing to get to the end, just like the first one. The killer's easier to pick out in this one than in the first book, though.<br /><br />The one thing I have a beef with is that being a Christian, I hate seeing God's name uncapitalized. If an author doesn't believe in God and doesn't want to offend readers, I think the author should have just written "oh my gosh" instead. Then again, I guess most people would figure Christians wouldn't be reading a book about magic in the first place...<br /><br />One word of advice: don't eat anything while reading this book! I did just that when I was beginning it and was grossed out by her describing how she puked and wipes the "spooge" off. There is a heck of a lot of vomiting going on in this book!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290949985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18394331633703434458">The first book of the series, Blue is for Nightmares, was okay. I found this novel to be basically a rehash of the first one, in terms of plot and character growth. Most of it dragged along and I found myself wanting to skip entire sections, particularly the extreme detail the author put into Stacey's New Age rituals. I suppose the book would be more appealing to junior high school students who also have an interest in Wicca. The ending was so obvious that I ended up skimming over it - yes, even</span>
  <span id="freeText18394331633703434458" style="display:none">The first book of the series, Blue is for Nightmares, was okay. I found this novel to be basically a rehash of the first one, in terms of plot and character growth. Most of it dragged along and I found myself wanting to skip entire sections, particularly the extreme detail the author put into Stacey's New Age rituals. I suppose the book would be more appealing to junior high school students who also have an interest in Wicca. The ending was so obvious that I ended up skimming over it - yes, even during the climax. Needless to say, this is the last book from this series that I'll be reading. I wasn't expecting much, but it was disappointing to find that something with what sounded like an interesting premise turned out to be about as dull and forgettable as the protagonist's name, Stacey Brown.</span>

  <span id="freeText14806102470389798266" style="display:none">I'm going to stop reading this. I've decided I don't really care about the characters or their ridiculous teen angst anymore. I don't really care for the writing style either. I'm pretty certain that Stacey's so-called 'BFF' is trying to steal her old boyfriend back from Stacey, that Stacey will end up with Jacob and that the ending will be as stupidly rushed as in the last book. It's like getting to the point of the end takes forever—"drawing out the suspense"—but the actual climax is so rushed, it's unsatisfying. I don't want to read 300 pages of this again to end up with the same feelings as I did in the first one. </span>

<div id="review_2491751001" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2491751001" />
    <a title="Donna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2465264-donna"><img alt="Donna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503933667p2/2465264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2491751001?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/2465264-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781417687060" href="/book/show/8532251-white-is-for-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=best-bitten">best-bitten</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2491751001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11091509279194424318">The second book in the Blue is for Nightmares series didn’t disappoint. WHITE IS FOR MAGIC delivers with even creepier dreams, projectile vomiting, and more rooted-in-reality magic that I can truly appreciate. It’s a more subtle fantasy and a subtle horror that plays with your head and I loved it.<br/><br/>I especially liked how unadjusted Drea was after everything. Which sounds twisted, but her reactions to things were so realistic and so honest that as a reader you really couldn’t fault her for them. Dr</span>
  <span id="freeText11091509279194424318" style="display:none">The second book in the Blue is for Nightmares series didn’t disappoint. WHITE IS FOR MAGIC delivers with even creepier dreams, projectile vomiting, and more rooted-in-reality magic that I can truly appreciate. It’s a more subtle fantasy and a subtle horror that plays with your head and I loved it.<br /><br />I especially liked how unadjusted Drea was after everything. Which sounds twisted, but her reactions to things were so realistic and so honest that as a reader you really couldn’t fault her for them. Drea went through hell and it left an indelible mark that meant Drea was not all gung ho to dive head first into Stacey’s nightmares all over again.<br /><br />I think Stacey’s dreams this time around were far creepier than in the first book and the stakes felt higher, but still realistic. The antagonists made a sick sort of sense, and were wholly infuriating for it. Demented though they were. But the line between insensitive yet harmless prank and very real threat was made unapologetically clear when Stacey started dreaming. And vomiting. Ugh. That is not a . . . skill? I would wish on anyone. I’d rather have the bed wetting, personally, I hate puking that much.<br /><br />Amber, for all her quirkiness, seemed to be the voice of reason a lot of the times here, supporting Stacey when she needed the support and trying to talk her off the ledge when Amber felt Stacey had gone a bit too far. When Stacey took liberties with their friendship, Amber was quick to remind her how crappy that was, because it wasn’t just Stacey that was at risk, it was all of them and Stacey getting hurt or killed would affect them all, something Stacey failed to remember a lot of the time.<br /><br />WHITE IS FOR MAGIC is the kind of story I like to read: fun (although it’s weird using that word to describe a horror novel about a kitchen witch who dreams about dead people), creepy, speaks to me but doesn’t leave me with an incredible hangover at the end of the book. It’s a book that’s to the point and won’t add fifteen pounds to my purse when I stick the book in there. It’s hard for me to describe books like this because they’re closer to the Fear Street type of books, but they’re far more substantive, there’s a lot more character development, there’s a lot more depth, but they’re not these epic tomes that I feel have overwhelmed the YA market lately. They’re the level of escapist I need without being overwhelmed by it. And I certainly have my fair share of tomes on my shelves, both having already read and waiting to be read, but I can’t have a significant emotional event after every book I read. I don’t have the energy for that.<br /><br />It’s funny because I was talking to a fellow YAck about that and she felt the same way, that YA right now is go big or go home. That if it’s not this epically deep doorstopper of a book then there’s no room for it. Probably literally because of all the 500 pages YA novels that keep coming out. I love me my Thanksgiving dinner, but I don’t have the energy to cook that every day, nor do I have the stomach to eat it every day. I think that’s why I fall back to these older books that sort of bridge that gap between first generation YA and now. Not only for the nostalgia factor but because they’re completely satisfying without being so incredibly emotionally overwhelming and I wish the current market had room for series like Blue is for Nightmares (and Morganville Vampires) again and I cross my fingers that they’ll eventually come back around. Luckily I do know editors are pushing for shorter YA because books have gotten so incredibly long so things are looking up.<br /><br />4.5</span>
  <a data-text-id="11091509279194424318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2351852310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2351852310" />
    <a title="Brooklyn Betts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59409846-brooklyn-betts"><img alt="Brooklyn Betts" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2351852310?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brooklyn Betts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brooklyn Betts" href="/user/show/59409846-brooklyn-betts">Brooklyn Betts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2351852310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2192179684302106748">The book "White is for Magic" was written by Laurie Faria Stolarz. It's about a seventeen year-old girl named Stacy who is starting to have nightmares of people who have been killed. She found out that the nightmares are telling her that she is going to die in less than a week, and needs to figure out how to survive. Someone named Jacob came to help her because he was having dreams about her death. At first Stacey doesn't trust him, but then she starts to fall in love with him, which causes prob</span>
  <span id="freeText2192179684302106748" style="display:none">The book "White is for Magic" was written by Laurie Faria Stolarz. It's about a seventeen year-old girl named Stacy who is starting to have nightmares of people who have been killed. She found out that the nightmares are telling her that she is going to die in less than a week, and needs to figure out how to survive. Someone named Jacob came to help her because he was having dreams about her death. At first Stacey doesn't trust him, but then she starts to fall in love with him, which causes problems with her current relationship and focus. With the help of her mother, memory of her dead grandmother, friends, and Jacob, she is able to prevent herself from being killed.<br /><br />I really liked the elements of mystery and romance in this book. When Stacey tried to find clues about her death, it was really interesting and fun to read because I was able to try and figure what might happen. The romance also was a good touch because there wasn't a lot of it, but there was a good amount of it which made the book really well put together. I didn't really like how some parts of the story were really repetitive. Some things kept happening over and over again which made some parts not very entertaining. I also wish it was a little more clear on some of the parts, because I couldn't really tell what was going on in some parts of the story. However, I really liked the book, and it's still one of my favorites.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to people who like mystery and a little bit of thriller. There were some parts of the book where it was very mysterious, and some parts were a little scary and make your heart race. I think young adults would really enjoy this book, and no one younger than that should read this book because there are more mature events and language that take place.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2192179684302106748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2402600152" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2402600152" />
    <a title="Patricia Brewer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74936561-patricia-brewer"><img alt="Patricia Brewer" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2402600152?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patricia Brewer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patricia Brewer" href="/user/show/74936561-patricia-brewer">Patricia Brewer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2402600152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3780905493026136679">White is for Magic by Laurie Faria Stolarz is truly a magical experience. It is about a girl named Stacey Brown who comes from a family of witches, significantly her grandma; who taught her everything she knows. She goes to a boarding school and although she’s roomed with her closest friends, she faces a serious rough patch with her need to graduate and her love life. As she deals with all of these day to day stresses, it just gets worse for her. She begins getting these premonitions, that had a</span>
  <span id="freeText3780905493026136679" style="display:none">White is for Magic by Laurie Faria Stolarz is truly a magical experience. It is about a girl named Stacey Brown who comes from a family of witches, significantly her grandma; who taught her everything she knows. She goes to a boarding school and although she’s roomed with her closest friends, she faces a serious rough patch with her need to graduate and her love life. As she deals with all of these day to day stresses, it just gets worse for her. She begins getting these premonitions, that had already once saved her friends life, but they get gruesome as she’s haunted by the fact that her saving her friends life, cost another person theirs. The premonitions tell her that she’s going to die, with the addition that she’d been receiving vague and utterly creepy letters from some anonymous person. Throughout the book Stacey meets a new student named Jacob who tries to warn her about her premonitions, and notifies her that he’d been getting them too. She forms a bond with him and struggles to not catch feelings for him considering her stumbling relationship of jealousy involving her best friend. The author does a good job of providing certain moments that really spark the chemistry between the two of them and show the tension that they both face when they first meet each other. Stolarz does a great job of arranging details and interpreting them in a way that foster moods and writing situations that readers can really understand and sympathize with. Though the book does have some setting flashbacks the author made them easy to understand the triggers of it and their significance. I would recommend this book to anyone who wants to experience the mystifying magic of the world Laurie Faria Stolarz created.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3780905493026136679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Dmx1Xns803st1uaSEcYtQmAf1TngVHsGtPGvous5tAk+eLkZ7FT2y4RXFUtOfxMH589xKN5iAv/IcZrjHlbD8w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uuiTgZSAuYrNeHHEqSz66VwUas5k4JfvztmyPup+/AiK/F/GA+icOmT5gh32lcSs28TO31rW7hayWYd/HxGL8g==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9169456266180932468">Laurie Faria Stolarz grew up in Salem, MA, attended Merrimack College, and received an MFA in Creative Writing from Emerson College in Boston. <br/><br/>Laurie Faria Stolarz is an American author of young adult fiction novels, best known for her Blue is for Nightmares series. Her works, which feature teenage protagonists, blend elements found in mystery and romance novels.<br/><br/>Stolarz found sales success with he</span>
  <span id="freeText9169456266180932468" style="display:none">Laurie Faria Stolarz grew up in Salem, MA, attended Merrimack College, and received an MFA in Creative Writing from Emerson College in Boston. <br /><br />Laurie Faria Stolarz is an American author of young adult fiction novels, best known for her Blue is for Nightmares series. Her works, which feature teenage protagonists, blend elements found in mystery and romance novels.<br /><br />Stolarz found sales success with her first novel, Blue is for Nightmares, and followed it up with three more titles in the series, White is for Magic, Silver is for Secrets, and Red is for Remembrance, as well as a companion graphic novel, Black is for Beginnings. Stolarz is also the author of the Touch series (Deadly Little Secret, Deadly Little Lies, Deadly Little Games, Deadly Little Voices, and Deadly Little Lessons), as well as Bleed and Project 17. With more than two million books sold worldwide, Stolarz's titles have been named on various awards list. </span>
